2:24:1340:0:14:72:437:700:12:Times:12:Times:A:Optimal Monetary Policy and the Sources of Local-Currency Price Stability
2:25:1413:14:14:72:324:686:12:Times:12:Times:A:Giancarlo Corsetti, Luca Dedola, and Sylvain Leduc
2:26:1463:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:A:NBER Working Paper No. 13544
2:27:1491:14:14:72:138:658:12:Times:12:Times:A:October 2007
2:28:1503:14:28:72:199:644:12:Times:12:Times:A:JEL No. F31,F33,F41,F42
2:29:1526:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:?:ABSTRACT
2:30:1534:28:14:72:540:588:12:Times:12:Times:A:We analyze the policy trade-offs generated by local currency price stability of imports in economies
2:31:1634:14:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:A:where upstream producers strategically interact with downstream firms selling the final goods to consumers.
2:32:1741:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:A:We study the effects of staggered price setting at the downstream level on the optimal price (and markup)
2:33:1846:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:A:chosen by upstream producers and show that downstream price movements affect the desired markup
2:34:1941:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:A:of upstream producers, magnifying their price response to shocks. We revisit the international dimensions
2:35:2046:14:14:72:540:518:12:Times:12:Times:A:of optimal monetary policy, unveiling an argument in favor of consumer price stability as the main
2:36:2144:14:14:72:540:504:12:Times:12:Times:A:prescription for monetary policy. Since stable consumer prices feed back into a low volatility of markups
2:37:2249:14:14:72:540:490:12:Times:12:Times:A:among upstream producers, this contains inefficient deviations from the law of one price at the border.
2:38:2352:14:14:72:540:476:12:Times:12:Times:A:However, efficient stabilization of different CPI components will not generally result into perfect stabilization
2:39:2465:14:14:72:540:462:12:Times:12:Times:A:of headline inflation. National policies optimally respond to the same shocks in a similar way, thus
2:40:2565:14:14:72:540:448:12:Times:12:Times:A:containing volatility of the terms of trade, but not necessarily of the real exchange rate. The latter will
2:41:2672:14:14:72:540:434:12:Times:12:Times:A:be more volatile, among other things, the larger the home bias in expenditure and the content of local
2:42:2774:14:42:72:198:420:12:Times:12:Times:A:inputs in consumer goods.
2:43:2799:42:14:72:160:378:12:Times:12:Times:A:Giancarlo Corsetti
2:44:2817:14:14:72:214:364:12:Times:12:Times:A:European University Institute
2:45:2846:14:14:72:156:350:12:Times:12:Times:A:Florence, ITALY
2:46:2861:14:28:72:190:336:12:Times:12:Times:A:giancarlo.corsetti@iue.it
2:47:2886:28:14:72:134:308:12:Times:12:Times:A:Luca Dedola
2:48:2897:14:14:72:223:294:12:Times:12:Times:A:Monetary Policy Research Div.
2:49:2926:14:14:72:185:280:12:Times:12:Times:A:European Central Bank
2:50:2947:14:14:72:158:266:12:Times:12:Times:A:Postfach 16 03 19
2:51:2964:14:14:72:282:252:12:Times:12:Times:A:D- 60066 Frankfurt am Manin GERMANY
2:52:2999:14:0:72:170:238:12:Times:12:Times:A:luca.dedola@ecb.int
2:53:3018:0:14:306:376:378:12:Times:12:Times:?:Sylvain Leduc
2:54:3031:14:14:306:436:364:12:Times:12:Times:?:Board of Governors of the 
2:55:3057:14:14:306:422:350:12:Times:12:Times:?:Federal Reserve System
2:56:3079:14:14:306:484:336:12:Times:12:Times:?:20th and C streets NW, Mail Stop 23
2:57:3114:14:14:306:420:322:12:Times:12:Times:?:Washington, DC 20551

3:59:3155:0:31:63:176:714:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:1  Introduction
3:60:3170:31:20:63:517:683:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The high degree of stability of import prices in local currency, documented both at the border
3:61:3264:20:21:63:517:663:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and at consumer level, vis--a-vis large movements in exchange rates, raises issues at the core of
3:62:3361:21:20:63:516:642:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the design of national monetary policies in a globalizing world economy.1On the one hand, a
3:63:3452:20:20:63:517:622:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:low elasticity of import prices with respect to the exchange rate can result from the presence
3:64:3546:20:21:63:517:602:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of costs incurred locally before the imported goods reach the consumers, such as distribution
3:65:3639:21:20:63:517:581:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:costs or assembling costs, i.e. costs of combining imported intermediated inputs with domestic
3:66:3733:20:20:63:517:561:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:inputs. By the same token, it may result from optimal markup adjustment by monopolistic
3:67:3820:20:21:63:517:541:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\frms, which maximize pro\fts through price discrimination across national markets (\pricing to
3:68:3915:21:20:63:517:520:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:market"). These are real sources of local-currency price stability of imports, which in\ruence
3:69:4009:20:20:63:517:500:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:pricing even in the absence of nominal rigidities. Although these factors may result in ine--
3:70:4102:20:20:63:517:480:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ciencies | like deviations from the law of one price due to pricing to market | they also shield
3:71:4198:20:21:63:517:460:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:price and wage dynamics from currency volatility, thus helping central banks maintain a low
3:72:4289:21:20:63:517:439:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and stable headline in\ration. On the other hand, stable import prices and low exchange rate
3:73:4381:20:20:63:517:419:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:pass-through can also stem from nominal frictions impeding desired markup adjustment, thus
3:74:4471:20:21:63:517:399:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:interfering with equilibrium movements in relative prices. When local-currency-price stability of
3:75:4568:21:20:63:517:378:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:imports is due to price stickiness, it creates policy trade-o-s between competing objectives, e.g.
3:76:4666:20:20:63:517:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:between stabilizing the prices of domestically produced goods as opposed to the (relative) price
3:77:4762:20:21:63:517:338:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of imported goods, which raise the importance of international considerations in the conduct of
3:78:4857:21:20:63:142:317:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:monetary policy.
3:79:4873:20:20:80:517:297:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In this paper we reconsider these policy trade-o-s in economies where stable import prices in
3:80:4966:20:21:63:517:277:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:local currency result from both nominal rigidities and endogenous destination-speci\fc markup
3:81:5059:21:20:63:517:256:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:adjustment. We specify a two country model where each economy produces an array of country-
3:82:5150:20:20:63:517:236:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:speci\fc, di-erentiated traded goods.  In each country, we model local downstream \frms as
3:83:5240:20:21:63:517:216:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:using one intermediate traded good, and possibly local inputs, to produce nontradable \fnal
3:84:5331:21:20:63:517:195:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:goods. In other words, each intermediate good is produced by an upstream monopolist and
3:85:5418:20:20:63:517:175:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:sold to a continuum of monopolistic downstream \frms, active in each country, from which local
3:86:5512:20:16:63:517:155:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consumers can directly buy further di-erentiated \fnal varieties. Thus, because both upstream
3:87:5605:16:21:75:517:139:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:1See, e.g., Engel and Rogers, [1996]; Goldberg and Knetter, [1997]; Campa and Goldberg, [2005] and Frankel
3:88:5711:21:0:63:114:118:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:et al. [2004].
4:89:5726:0:20:63:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and downstream \frms have monopoly power, \fnal prices re\rect double marginalization. We
4:90:5815:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:posit that markets are segmentated across national borders, so that intermediate producers price-
4:91:5912:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:discriminate between domestic and foreign local downstream producers as a group, although not
4:92:6005:21:20:63:471:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:among individual local producers (charging di-erent prices within the same country).
4:93:6089:20:20:80:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:As in standard monetary models, we assume that \frms set prices in local currency, adjusting
4:94:6181:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:them infrequently according to the Calvo mechanism.2Di-erent from the previous literature,
4:95:6271:21:20:63:517:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:however, we explicitly model strategic interactions among upstream and downstream \frms:
4:96:6359:20:20:63:517:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:upstream \frms exercise their monopoly power by taking into account country-speci\fc di-erences
4:97:6454:20:21:63:517:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the properties of the demand for their products. Relative to the literature already modelling
4:98:6550:21:20:63:517:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:vertical interactions between exporters and local \frms (e.g. Bacchetta and Van Wincoop [2005],
4:99:6645:20:20:63:517:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Corsetti and Dedola [2005], Devereux and Engel [2007], Monacelli [2005]), an important novel
4:100:6737:20:21:63:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:contribution of this paper consists of analyzing the e-ects of staggered price setting at the
4:101:6830:21:20:63:467:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:downstream level on the optimal price (and markup) chosen by upstream producers.
4:102:6910:20:20:80:517:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Speci\fcally, our analysis establishes three key characteristics of the perceived demand elas-
4:103:7004:20:21:63:517:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ticity by upstream producers when nominal rigidities constrain price decisions by downstream
4:104:7096:21:20:63:517:409:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\frms.First, this elasticity is a decreasing function of the rate of change of \fnal prices in each
4:105:7195:20:20:63:517:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:industry: the higher this rate (thus the higher the price dispersion among \fnal producers selling
4:106:7293:20:21:63:516:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:an industry product), the higher the intermediate producer's equilibrium markup.Second, the
4:107:7384:21:20:63:517:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:perceived demand elasticity is market-speci\fc, depending on di-erences in industry-speci\fc in-
4:108:7480:20:20:63:517:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\ration rates across the domestic and the export market. Sticky prices at consumer level create
4:109:7575:20:21:63:517:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:an incentive for upstream \frms to price discriminate across borders, which leads to equilibrium
4:110:7671:21:20:63:517:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:deviations from the law of one price, independently of the degree of nominal rigidities in the
4:111:7765:20:20:63:516:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:upstream \frms' own prices.Third, if either local inputs in downstream production are good
4:112:7855:20:21:63:517:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:substitute of intermediate imported goods, or their share in the downstream \frms' costs is low,
4:113:7951:21:20:63:517:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the demand elasticity is decreasing in the price charged by upstream producers. In other words,
4:114:8046:20:20:63:517:206:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:downstream nominal rigidities magnify the price response to shocks by upstream monopolists
4:115:8136:20:21:63:517:186:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:who optimally reset their price in any given period. This generates strategic substitutability
4:116:8230:21:20:63:517:165:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:among upstream producers: a rise in marginal costs will lead to an increase in their desired
4:117:8322:20:20:63:107:145:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:markups.
4:118:8330:20:0:75:257:125:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:?:2See the literature review in section 2 below.
5:119:8377:0:20:80:516:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:These results have at least two notable implications for policy modelling and design.First, by
5:120:8471:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:shedding light on the link between optimal price adjustment at the dock and domestic in\ration
5:121:8565:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rates, our results suggest a speci\fc reason why, in line with the observations by Taylor [2000],
5:122:8662:21:20:63:517:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:lower CPI in\ration volatility and price dispersion may result in a lower degree of exchange-
5:123:8755:20:20:63:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rate pass-through: stable in\ration reduces at the margin the producers' incentives to price
5:124:8847:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:discriminate across countries, decreasing the sensitivity of their `desired markup' to cost changes.
5:125:8947:21:20:80:516:592:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f3:A:Second, by showing that downstream price rigidities result into strategic substitutability
5:126:9037:20:20:63:517:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:among upstream producers, our results emphasize that adding several layers of nominal rigidi-
5:127:9130:20:21:63:517:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ties do not necessarily results into more price inertia. Strategic interactions among vertically
5:128:9226:21:20:63:517:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:integrated \frms with sticky prices may create incentive for large price adjustment, feeding back
5:129:9323:20:20:63:173:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:into in\ration volatility.
5:130:9349:20:21:80:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In addition, our model speci\fcation implies an important dimension of heterogeneity across
5:131:9440:21:20:63:517:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\frms which has a bearing on optimal monetary policy.  In contrast to standard models, the
5:132:9530:20:20:63:517:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:marginal costs of our downstream \frms are generally not symmetric, not even when the economy
5:133:9623:20:21:63:517:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is completely closed to foreign trade and there are no markup shocks. Thus, monetary authorities
5:134:9719:21:20:63:354:409:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:are not able to achieve complete stabilization of \fnal prices.3
5:135:9783:20:20:80:517:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The mechanism underlying these results is di-erent from that emphasized by the previous
5:136:9870:20:21:63:517:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:literature focusing on vertical interactions between upstream and downstream \frms, but that
5:137:9962:21:20:63:517:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:stresses real determinants of the local currency price stability of imports. In previous work of
5:138:10058:20:20:63:517:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ours, we assume that local \frms produce consumer goods by combining intermediate tradable
5:139:10148:20:21:63:517:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:goods with local inputs (Corsetti and Dedola [2005], Corsetti, Dedola, and Leduc [2007]). In
5:140:10240:21:20:63:517:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:this framework, provided that the tradable goods and the local inputs are poor substitutes
5:141:10330:20:20:63:517:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in production, the presence of local inputs tends to mute the response of upstream prices to
5:142:10422:20:21:63:517:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:shocks (corresponding to a case of strategic complementarity), and makes the exchange-rate
5:143:10512:21:20:63:517:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:pass-through incomplete, even in the absence of nominal rigidities. Building an example of an
5:144:10605:20:20:63:517:206:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:economy encompassing both channels, we analyze conditions under which the properties of the
5:145:10696:20:21:63:517:186:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:demand elasticity faced by upstream producers are dominated by the e-ect of local inputs in
5:146:10787:21:15:63:398:165:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:production, as opposed to the e-ect of downstream nominal rigidities.
5:147:10856:15:21:75:517:150:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:3In standard models with cost-push and markup shocks, monetary authorities can achieve complete price
5:148:10957:21:16:63:517:129:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:stability, but face trade-o-s that motivate deviations from it | see for instance the discussion in Woodford
5:149:11065:16:0:63:377:113:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:[2003]. In our model, instead, stability of all prices is unfeasible to start with.
6:150:11149:0:20:80:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We characterize the optimal cooperative monetary policy under commitment. In order to
6:151:11234:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:reduce ine-ciencies due to price stickiness, monetary policy does mitigate \ructuations in the
6:152:11328:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:major components of consumer price in\ration. However, it falls short of stabilizing completely
6:153:11423:21:20:63:353:653:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:either the CPI, or the price of domestic intermediate goods.4
6:154:11484:20:20:80:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Optimal monetary policies address di-erent trade-o-s, speci\fc to both the international and
6:155:11576:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the domestic dimensions of the economy. First, as in Corsetti and Pesenti [2005], nominal rigidi-
6:156:11673:21:20:63:517:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ties in local currency at upstream level lead benevolent monetary authorities to attach a positive
6:157:11771:20:20:63:517:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:weight to stabilizing the consumer price of imports, and thus deviate from perfect stabilization
6:158:11867:20:21:63:517:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the \fnal prices of domestic goods. Second, downstream technology shocks prevent perfect
6:159:11958:21:20:63:517:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:stabilization of all consumer prices, because vertical interactions with upstream \frms, which
6:160:12052:20:20:63:517:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:may or may not adjust their prices, induce heterogeneity of marginal costs at retail level. This
6:161:12148:20:21:63:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:e-ect is compounded in an open economy setting, because of the response of the intermediate
6:162:12239:21:20:63:517:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:price of imports to exchange rate \ructuations. Third, the elasticity of the producer's demand
6:163:12333:20:20:63:517:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:curve falls with the industry's dispersion of \fnal goods prices, motivating policy emphasis on
6:164:12428:20:21:63:175:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\fnal price stabilization.
6:165:12454:21:20:80:517:409:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:None of these trade-o-s, however, entail speci\fc prescriptions regarding the volatility of the
6:166:12549:20:20:63:517:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:real exchange rate. In the literature, optimal monetary policy in models with nominal rigidities
6:167:12645:20:21:63:517:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in local currency is sometimes associated with a limited degree of real exchange rate volatility,
6:168:12742:21:20:63:517:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:relative to the terms of trade | see e.g. Devereux and Engel [2007]. In contrast, we \fnd that
6:169:12836:20:20:63:517:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:implementing the optimal policy in our economy with nominal rigidities leads the real exchange
6:170:12930:20:21:63:517:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rate to be more volatile, and the terms of trade to be less volatile, than in the same economy
6:171:13024:21:20:63:517:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:under \rexible prices.  This is because of the combined e-ects of nominal rigidities, and the
6:172:13117:20:20:63:517:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:presence of nontradable components in \fnal goods. We take these \fndings as a caution against
6:173:13211:20:21:63:517:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:strong policy prescriptions on the need to curb the volatility of the real exchange rate. The
6:174:13304:21:20:63:517:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:point is that, while there are good reasons to expect optimal policies to contain the volatility
6:175:13400:20:20:63:517:206:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the terms of trade, these reasons cannot be mechanically extended to the real exchange rate,
6:176:13495:20:21:63:479:186:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:whose volatility is bound to depend on a number of structural features of the economy.
6:177:13581:21:15:80:517:165:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:This paper is organized as follows. In the next section, we will brie\ry survey the literature
6:178:13675:15:21:75:517:150:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:4In our model economy the isomorphism between optimal monetary policy in closed and open economies
6:179:13773:21:16:63:517:129:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:characterized by Clarida, Gal-- and Gertler [2002] obviously does not hold, as policymakers face several trade-o-s
6:180:13887:16:0:63:329:113:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:which make perfect stabilization of domestic in\ration suboptimal.
7:181:13954:0:20:63:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:on pricing to market and monetary policy, with the goal of clarifying our contributions to it.
7:182:14048:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Section 3 speci\fes the model, while Section 4 provides analytical results on the link between
7:183:14142:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:price stickiness and price discrimination arising from vertical interactions. Section 5 describes
7:184:14239:21:20:63:517:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:our calibration of the model. Section 6 presents the equilibrium dynamics of prices in response to
7:185:14337:20:20:63:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:shocks, while Section 7 discusses the allocation under the optimal policy, relative to alternative
7:186:14435:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:policy rules and the case of \rexible prices. Section 8 concludes. An appendix provides analytical
7:187:14533:21:43:63:348:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:details on the model and the derivation of the main results.
7:188:14593:43:27:63:517:549:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:F:2  Local currency price stability and e-cient monetary stabi-
7:189:14654:27:31:87:139:522:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:A:lization
7:190:14662:31:20:63:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:In this section we brie\ry reconstruct the main development of recent debates on the local cur-
7:191:14757:20:21:63:517:471:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rency price stability of imports, and their implications for the international transmission and the
7:192:14856:21:20:63:517:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:optimal design of monetary policy, with the goal of clarifying our contribution to the literature.
7:193:14954:20:20:63:517:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:A core issue underlying these debates is whether monetary policy should react to international
7:194:15048:20:21:63:517:410:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:variables, such as the exchange rate or the terms of trade, beyond the in\ruence that these vari-
7:195:15145:21:20:63:517:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ables have on the domestic output gap (for example, via external demand) and on the domestic
7:196:15237:20:20:63:517:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:good prices | so that it would have a speci\fc `international dimension.' As discussed below,
7:197:15330:20:21:63:517:349:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:models stressing the stability of import prices in local currency have provided one possible an-
7:198:15426:21:20:63:517:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:swer to this question stressing the implications of nominal rigidities for monetary transmission
7:199:15522:20:36:63:177:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and stabilization policy.
7:200:15547:36:21:63:517:272:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:F:2.1  Nominal rigidities and the international dimensions of optimal monetary
7:201:15623:21:27:94:129:251:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:policy
7:202:15629:27:21:63:517:224:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:At the heart of the international dimension of monetary policy lies the role of the exchange
7:203:15721:21:20:63:517:203:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rate in the international transmission mechanism. Consistent with traditional open macroeco-
7:204:15813:20:20:63:517:183:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:nomic models, the seminal contribution to the New Open Economy Macroeconomics (henceforth
7:205:15902:20:21:63:517:163:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:NOEM) by Obstfeld and Rogo- [1995] embraces the view that exchange rate movements play
7:206:15988:21:20:63:517:142:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the stabilizing role of adjusting international relative prices in response to shocks, when frictions
7:207:16089:20:20:63:517:122:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:prevent or slow down price adjustment in the local currency. The idea is that nominal depre-
7:208:16181:20:0:63:517:102:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ciation transpires into real depreciation, making domestic goods cheaper in the world markets,
8:209:16276:0:20:63:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:hence redirecting world demand towards them: exchange rate movements therefore have `ex-
8:210:16364:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:penditure switching e-ects'. Accordingly, NOEM contributions after Obstfeld and Rogo- [1995]
8:211:16456:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:draw on the Mundell{Fleming and Keynesian tradition, and posit that \frms preset the price for
8:212:16550:21:20:63:517:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:their products in domestic currency, implying that export prices are sticky in the currency of
8:213:16644:20:20:63:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the producers | this is why such hypothesis is commonly dubbed `producer currency pricing'
8:214:16734:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(henceforth PCP). Under this hypothesis, nominal import prices in local currency move one-to-
8:215:16827:21:20:63:517:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:one with the exchange rate and pass-through is perfect. In the baseline model with preset prices,
8:216:16924:20:20:63:517:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to the extent that the demand elasticities are identical across countries, there is no incentive
8:217:17020:20:21:63:517:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for producers to charge di-erent prices in di-erent markets: in equilibrium there would be no
8:218:17113:21:20:63:435:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:deviations from the law of one price even if national markets were segmented.
8:219:17190:20:20:80:517:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In model economies with PCP, optimal monetary policy rules tend to be `inward-looking' and
8:220:17280:20:21:63:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:`iso-morphic' to the rules derived in closed-economy models: welfare-maximizing central banks
8:221:17373:21:20:63:517:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:pursue the stabilization of domestic producers marginal costs and markups | hence they aim
8:222:17463:20:20:63:517:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:at stabilizing the GDP de\rator |, while letting the consumer price index (CPI) \ructuate with
8:223:17557:20:21:63:517:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:e-cient movements in the relative price of imports. There is no need for monetary policies to
8:224:17650:21:20:63:517:409:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:react to international variables | a result that in the baseline NOEM model after Corsetti and
8:225:17744:20:20:63:517:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Pesenti [2001] goes through under di-erent assumptions regarding nominal rigidities, including
8:226:17838:20:21:63:517:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:staggered price setting and partial adjustment (see, for example, Clarida, Gal-- and Gertler
8:227:17930:21:20:63:452:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:[2002], or Benigno and Benigno [2003] for a generalization of the baseline model).
8:228:18012:20:20:80:517:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The high elasticity of import prices to the exchange rate underlying the contributions after
8:229:18104:20:21:63:517:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Obstfeld and Rogo- [1995], however, is clearly at odds with a large body of empirical studies
8:230:18197:21:20:63:517:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:showing that the exchange rate pass-through on import prices is far from complete in the short
8:231:18291:20:20:63:517:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:run, and deviations from the law of one price are large and persistent (see, for example, Engel
8:232:18386:20:21:63:517:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and Rogers [1996]; Goldberg and Knetter [1997]; Campa and Goldberg [2005]). Based on this
8:233:18475:21:20:63:517:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:evidence, several contributions have engaged in a thorough critique of the received wisdom on
8:234:18568:20:20:63:517:206:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the expenditure switching e-ects of the exchange rate. Speci\fcally, Betts and Devereux [2000]
8:235:18662:20:21:63:517:186:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and Devereux and Engel [2003], among others, posit that \frms preset export prices in the
8:236:18751:21:20:63:517:165:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:currency of the market where they sell their goods. This assumption, commonly dubbed `local
8:237:18842:20:20:63:517:145:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:currency pricing' (henceforth LCP), attributes local currency price stability of imports entirely
8:238:18939:20:21:63:517:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to nominal frictions. The far-reaching implications of LCP for the role of the exchange rate in
8:239:19034:21:0:63:517:104:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the international transmission mechanism have been widely discussed by the literature (see e.g.
9:240:19130:0:20:63:129:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Engel [2003]).
9:241:19144:20:20:80:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:To the extent that import prices are sticky in the local currency, a Home depreciation does
9:242:19235:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:not a-ect the price of Home goods in the world markets; hence, it has no expenditure switching
9:243:19329:21:20:63:517:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:e-ects.  Instead, it raises the ex-post markups on Home exports:  at given marginal costs,
9:244:19419:20:20:63:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:revenues in domestic currency from selling goods abroad rise.  In contrast with the received
9:245:19511:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:wisdom, nominal depreciation strengthens a country's terms of trade: if export prices are preset
9:246:19607:21:20:63:485:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:during the period, the Home terms of trade improves when the Home currency weakens.
9:247:19690:20:20:80:517:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:As opposed to earlier literature, models assuming LCP unveil a clear-cut argument in favour
9:248:19781:20:21:63:517:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of policies with an `international dimension.' One way to present the argument is as follows.
9:249:19874:21:20:63:517:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:To the extent that exporters' revenues and markups are exposed to exchange rate uncertainty,
9:250:19966:20:20:63:517:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\frms' optimal pricing strategies internalize the monetary policy of the importing country. In the
9:251:20064:20:21:63:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:benchmark model by Corsetti and Pesenti [2005], for instance, foreign \frms optimally preset the
9:252:20160:21:20:63:517:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:price of their goods in the Home market one period ahead, by charging the equilibrium markup
9:253:20252:20:20:63:517:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:over expected marginal costs evaluated in Home currency. The preset price of Home imports
9:254:20341:20:21:63:517:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:then depends on the joint distribution of Home monetary policy and Foreign productivity shocks:
9:255:20436:21:20:63:403:409:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the model, it is increasing in the variance of nominal marginal costs.
9:256:20509:20:20:80:517:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The reason why the isomorphism between closed-economy and open-economy monetary rules
9:257:20594:20:21:63:517:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:breaks down is apparent. Suppose that the Home monetary authorities ignore the in\ruence of
9:258:20685:21:20:63:517:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:their decisions on the price of Home imports. Incomplete stabilization of Foreign \frms marginal
9:259:20781:20:20:63:517:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:costs and markup in local currency will translate into ine-ciently high local prices of their
9:260:20874:20:21:63:517:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:product (relative to their level in the \rexible-price allocation). On the other hand, if Home
9:261:20968:21:20:63:517:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:monetary authorities wanted to stabilize Foreign \frms' marginal costs, they could only do so
9:262:21061:20:20:63:517:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:at the cost of raising costs and markup uncertainty for Home producers, resulting in ine-cient
9:263:21155:20:21:63:517:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Home good prices.  It follows that, to maximize Home welfare, Home policymakers should
9:264:21241:21:20:63:517:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:optimally trade-o- the stabilization of marginal costs of all producers (domestic and foreign)
9:265:21335:20:20:63:517:206:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:selling in the Home markets. The optimal response to Foreign shocks by domestic policymakers
9:266:21427:20:21:63:517:186:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:depends, among other factors, on the degree of openness of the economy, as indexed by the
9:267:21516:21:20:63:517:165:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:overall share of imports in the CPI (see Corsetti and Pesenti [2005], and Sutherland [2005], for
9:268:21612:20:20:63:318:145:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a discussion of intermediate degrees of pass-through).
9:269:21666:20:21:80:517:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In section 7 of this paper we will show that these basic principles of the `international
9:270:21755:21:0:63:517:104:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:dimensions of optimal monetary policies' go through in models assuming LCP and staggered
10:271:21844:0:20:63:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:price adjustment. Namely, in our model monetary authorities will optimally attempt to stabilize
10:272:21939:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the CPI, although CPI stabilization will not be complete because of the asymmetry in shocks
10:273:22030:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:hitting di-erent economies and di-erent sectors of the same national economy, creating the need
10:274:22125:21:20:63:517:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for relative price adjustment. At an optimum, welfare-maximizing policymakers will thus trade-
10:275:22219:20:20:63:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:o- ine-cient misalignment of import prices, with ine-cient relative price dispersion among
10:276:22309:20:36:63:480:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:domestic and foreign goods (see also Smets and Wouters, [2002], and Monacelli [2005]).
10:277:22395:36:21:63:517:577:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:F:2.2  Interactions of nominal and real determinants of local currency price
10:278:22469:21:28:94:207:556:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:stability of imports
10:279:22489:28:20:63:517:528:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:While most of the discussion in the NOEM literature has focused on incomplete pass-through as
10:280:22582:20:20:63:517:508:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:an implication of nominal rigidities, a low pass-through, in itself, is not necessarily incompatible
10:281:22682:20:21:63:517:488:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:with expenditure switching e-ects | a point stressed by Obstfeld [2000] among others.  In
10:282:22771:21:20:63:517:467:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:this respect, Obstfeld and Rogo- [2000] points out that, in the data (and consistent with the
10:283:22864:20:20:63:517:447:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:received wisdom), nominal depreciation does tend to be associated with deteriorating terms of
10:284:22957:20:21:63:517:427:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:trade. This piece of evidence clearly sets an empirical hurdle for LCP models: speci\fcations
10:285:23050:21:20:63:517:406:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:which assume a very high degree of price stickiness in local currency cannot pass this test (see
10:286:23146:20:20:63:517:386:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Corsetti, Dedola, and Leduc [2005], for a quantitative assessment).  Interestingly, estimates
10:287:23239:20:21:63:517:366:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of LCP models attributing incomplete pass-through exclusively to nominal rigidities in local
10:288:23331:21:20:63:517:345:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:currency, tend to predict that the degree of price stickiness is implausibly higher for imports
10:289:23426:20:20:63:517:325:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:than for domestic goods | a result suggesting model misspeci\fcation (see, for example, Lubik
10:290:23519:20:21:63:178:305:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and Schorfheide [2006]).
10:291:23543:21:20:80:517:284:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The key issue is the extent to which the evidence of local currency price stability of imports
10:292:23637:20:20:63:517:264:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:can be explained by nominal rigidities.  In the literature, it is well understood that the low
10:293:23731:20:21:63:517:244:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:elasticity of import prices at the retail level with respect to the exchange rate is in large part
10:294:23829:21:20:63:517:223:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:due to the incidence of distribution (see Burstein, Eichenbaum, and Rebelo [2006] for a recent
10:295:23923:20:20:63:517:203:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:reconsideration of this point). Namely suppose that import prices at the dock move one-to-one
10:296:24016:20:20:63:517:183:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:with the exchange rate, but the distribution margin account for 50 percent of the retail price,
10:297:24111:20:21:63:517:163:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:mostly covering local costs. A one percent depreciation of the currency will then a-ect the \fnal
10:298:24208:21:20:63:292:142:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:price of the imported good only by 1/2 percent.
10:299:24255:20:20:80:517:122:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In addition, several macro and micro contributions have emphasized that import prices at
10:300:24343:20:0:63:517:102:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the dock do not move one-to-one with the exchange rate because of optimal destination-speci\fc
11:301:24438:0:20:63:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:markup adjustment by monopolistic \frms. Instances of these studies include Dornbusch [1987],
11:302:24531:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:stressing market structure, as well as previous work by two of us (Corsetti and Dedola [2005]),
11:303:24626:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:where upstream monopolists sell their tradable goods to downstream \frms, which combine them
11:304:24718:21:20:63:517:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:with local inputs before reaching the consumer. The latter contribution establishes that, to the
11:305:24814:20:20:63:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:extent that the tradable goods and the local inputs are not good substitutes in the downstream
11:306:24908:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\frms' production, the demand elasticity faced by upstream monopolists will be (a) market spe-
11:307:25002:21:20:63:517:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ci\fc, causing optimal price discrimination across markets, and (b) increasing in the monopolists
11:308:25099:20:20:63:517:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:price, thus leading to incomplete exchange rate pass-through independently of nominal rigidities.
11:309:25196:20:21:63:517:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Based on this principle, that paper then generalizes the model with distribution by Burstein,
11:310:25289:21:20:63:517:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Neves and Rebelo [2003], as to encompass local currency price stability due to endogenous move-
11:311:25384:20:20:63:517:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ments of markups implied by the presence of distribution services intensive in local inputs. The
11:312:25480:20:21:63:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:same principle nonetheless can be applied to models where intermediate imported inputs are
11:313:25570:21:20:63:517:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:assembled using local inputs | a case analyzed by Bacchetta and Van Wincoop 2003. Whether
11:314:25659:20:20:63:517:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:one has in mind markets with high distribution margins (such as the market for cups of co-ee
11:315:25751:20:21:63:517:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:at Starbucks in the US), or markets for goods with a relatively high incidence of imported parts
11:316:25847:21:20:63:517:409:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:(such as the market for cars `made in the US'), incomplete exchange rate pass through can be
11:317:25939:20:20:63:517:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:traced back to some degree of complementarity between imported goods and local input/services.
11:318:26033:20:21:80:517:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Analyses of the relative importance of these di-erent sources of import price stability (espe-
11:319:26127:21:20:63:517:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:cially local costs) are provided by several market-speci\fc studies | such as Goldberg and Ver-
11:320:26222:20:20:63:517:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:boven [2001], Goldberg and Hellerstein [2007], and Hellerstein [2006]. The main result emerging
11:321:26317:20:21:63:517:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:from these partial-equilibrium contributions is that real factors can explain a large extent of local
11:322:26418:21:20:63:517:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:currency price stability of imports. Most interestingly, similar conclusions can be reached using
11:323:26515:20:20:63:517:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:quantitative, general equilibrium models, as suggested by the numerical exercises in Corsetti
11:324:26608:20:21:63:152:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and Dedola [2005].
11:325:26626:21:20:80:517:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Yet, quantitative studies incorporating these factors also corroborate the idea that a realistic
11:326:26722:20:20:63:517:206:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:degree of nominal rigidities can improve substantially the performance of the model. In Corsetti,
11:327:26819:20:21:63:517:186:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Dedola, and Leduc [2005], we show that a model assuming LCP together with vertical interaction
11:328:26913:21:20:63:517:165:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:between producers and distributors can pass the empirical hurdle set by Obstfeld and Rogo-
11:329:27003:20:20:63:517:145:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:[2000], provided that the average frequency of price adjustment is consistent with the evidence
11:330:27098:20:21:63:194:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:by Bils and Klenow (2004).
11:331:27124:21:0:80:517:104:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Research is therefore increasingly focused on the interaction between real and monetary
12:332:27212:0:20:63:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:determinants of low exchange rate pass-through and deviations from the law of one price. A
12:333:27302:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\frst early instance of research focused on such interaction is provided by contributions which
12:334:27397:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:emphasize the need to treat the currency denomination of exports as an endogenous choice by
12:335:27488:21:20:63:517:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:pro\ft maximizing \frms. Bacchetta and Van Wincoop [2005], Devereux, Engel and Storgaard
12:336:27576:20:20:63:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:[2004], and Friberg [1998] have developed models where \frms can choose whether to price export
12:337:27671:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in domestic or in foreign currency, knowing that price updates will be subject to frictions. A
12:338:27765:21:20:63:517:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:number of factors | from the market share of exporters to the incidence of distribution, and
12:339:27857:20:20:63:517:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the availability of hedging instruments | potentially play a crucial role in this choice (see Engel
12:340:27956:20:21:63:173:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:[2006], for a synthesis).
12:341:27981:21:20:80:517:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Although most of these models are developed assuming an arbitrary monetary policy, the
12:342:28067:20:20:63:517:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:role of optimal stabilization policy in the choice between LCP and PCP is addressed by Corsetti
12:343:28162:20:21:63:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and Pesenti [2001]. The main idea is that expansionary monetary shocks unrelated to funda-
12:344:28252:21:20:63:517:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:mental shocks (e.g. productivity) raise nominal wages and marginal costs while depreciating the
12:345:28347:20:20:63:517:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:currency. Consider a \frm located in a country with noisy monetary policy, i.e. hit by frequent
12:346:28442:20:21:63:517:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:monetary shocks unrelated to fundamentals. For such \frm, pricing its exports in foreign cur-
12:347:28535:21:20:63:517:409:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rency (that is, choosing LCP) is attractive in the following sense: it ensures that revenues from
12:348:28632:20:20:63:517:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:exports in domestic currency will move in parallel with nominal marginal costs, with stabilizing
12:349:28728:20:21:63:517:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:e-ects on the markup. This is because any expansionary monetary shock depreciating the Home
12:350:28819:21:20:63:517:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:currency would simultaneously raise wages and the domestic currency revenue from unit sales
12:351:28910:20:20:63:517:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:abroad (at an unchanged local price). This observation may help explain why exporters from
12:352:29000:20:21:63:517:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:countries with relatively unstable domestic monetary policies (e.g. some developing countries)
12:353:29094:21:20:63:517:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:prefer to price their exports to developed countries in the importers' currency. The same argu-
12:354:29189:20:20:63:517:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ment, however, suggests that LCP is not necessarily optimal for exporters producing in countries
12:355:29285:20:21:63:517:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:where monetary policy systematically stabilizes marginal costs (see Goldberg and Tille [2005],
12:356:29379:21:20:63:517:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for empirical evidence). For \frms located in these countries, real factors arguably become more
12:357:29475:20:20:63:168:206:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:relevant in the choice.
12:358:29498:20:21:80:517:186:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:A second instance of the new directions taken by the literature consists of studies taking
12:359:29588:21:20:63:517:165:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the LCP choice as given, and combining it with di-erent determinants of pricing to market and
12:360:29681:20:20:63:517:145:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:incomplete pass-through. This is the approach we take in this paper. In contrast from previous
12:361:29775:20:21:63:517:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:contributions, where price stickiness is not linked to price discrimination (see e.g. Monacelli
12:362:29870:21:0:63:517:104:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:[2005]), or where nominal rigidities and price discrimination coexist without feeding into each
13:363:29967:0:20:63:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:other (see e.g.  Corsetti, Dedola, and Leduc [2005]), we specify a model building on the in-
13:364:30059:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tuitive idea that the frequency of price changes by local downstream \frms selling products
13:365:30150:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to consumers, is bound to a-ect the elasticity of demand perceived by upstream producers
13:366:30238:21:20:63:517:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of intermediate (tradable inputs or) goods. The novel result of our study is that, looking at
13:367:30331:20:20:63:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the interactions between nominal and real determinants of price discrimination in an otherwise
13:368:30425:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:standard monetary model, nominal rigidities at the retail level do not necessarily lower the
13:369:30517:21:20:63:517:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium reaction of \fnal prices to exchange rate movements, thus increasing price inertia.
13:370:30612:20:20:63:517:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:As mentioned in the Introduction, downstream price rigidities tend to generate strategic substi-
13:371:30708:20:21:63:517:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tutability among upstream producers and an overall larger sensitivity of all prices to exchange
13:372:30803:21:43:63:125:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rate changes.
13:373:30816:43:31:63:229:488:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3  The model economy
13:374:30836:31:21:63:516:457:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The world economy consists of two countries of equal size,HandF. Each country specializes
13:375:30925:21:20:63:517:436:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in one type of tradable good, produced in a number of di-erentiated industries de\fned over a
13:376:31018:20:20:63:517:416:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:continuum of unit mass. Tradable goods are indexed byh2[0;1] in the Home country and
13:377:31102:20:20:63:517:396:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f3:B:f2[0;1] in the Foreign country. In each industry, the \frm producing the tradable goodh(or
13:378:31192:20:21:63:517:376:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f3:B:f) is a monopolistic supplier of one good, using labor as the only input to production. These
13:379:31285:21:20:63:466:355:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\frms set prices in local currency units and in a staggered fashion as in Calvo [1983].
13:380:31372:20:20:80:517:335:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:A distinctive feature of our setting is that we model a downstream sector in each country.
13:381:31462:20:21:63:516:315:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Speci\fcally, we assume that each producer's goodhis sold to consumers in many varieties by a
13:382:31555:21:20:63:517:294:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:continuum of local \frms indexed byrh2[0;1]:These \frms buy thehtradable goods, and turn
13:383:31643:20:20:63:517:274:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:them into consumer goods | which are not traded across borders | with random productivity.
13:384:31733:20:21:63:517:254:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We will distinguish between two cases: one in which local \frms use domestic labor as an input;
13:385:31828:21:20:63:517:233:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the other in which they do not. Similar to upstream producers, also downstream operate under
13:386:31920:20:20:63:452:213:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:monopolistic competition and set prices in a staggered fashion as in Calvo [1983].
13:387:32002:20:21:80:517:193:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:By the logic of the Calvo adjustment, local downstream \frms buying goods from upstream
13:388:32089:21:20:63:517:172:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:producers charge di-erent prices to \fnal users, with a constant fraction of them reoptimizing
13:389:32183:20:20:63:517:152:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:prices in each period. In principle, one could assume that upstream \frms exercise their monopoly
13:390:32280:20:21:63:517:132:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:power by charging individual prices which are speci\fc to each downstream \frm. However, we
13:391:32371:21:0:63:517:111:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\fnd it more realistic and convincing to assume that upstream producers are not able to price-
14:392:32467:0:20:63:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:discriminate across individual local \frms, but only across groups of them | namely, across
14:393:32558:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:domestic and foreign local \frms. So, we assume that upstream producers exercise their monopoly
14:394:32653:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:power and set prices by taking into account the total demand for their product in each market,
14:395:32747:21:20:63:238:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:at Home and in the Foreign country.
14:396:32782:20:20:80:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In what follows, we describe our set up focusing on the Home country, with the understanding
14:397:32874:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that similar expressions also characterize the Foreign economy | variables referred to Foreign
14:398:32968:21:35:63:303:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\frms and households are marked with an asterisk.

24:1099:52086:20:20:63:517:169:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:knows that a fraction 1--of them will do so, while a fraction-will keep their price unchanged.
24:1100:52180:20:21:63:517:149:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Because of the latter, the upstream producers will optimally respond to shocks to own marginal
24:1101:52274:21:20:63:517:128:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:costs by charging a price which is higher than she/he would ideally charge if all downstream

32:1654:65967:36:28:63:210:333:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.2  Productivity shocks

33:1670:66998:37:27:63:191:637:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:5.3  Monetary policy

33:1674:67298:20:20:63:517:549:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the planner places equal weights on Home and Foreign welfare, so that world welfare is given by
