34:1696:68781:0:31:63:494:714:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:6  The response of producers and consumer prices to shocks
34:1697:68839:31:20:63:517:683:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:In this section, we use our quantitative framework to discuss key properties of our model re-
34:1698:68932:20:21:63:517:663:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:garding the behavior of prices and markups in response to productivity shocks. Figures 1 and 2
34:1699:69026:21:20:63:517:642:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:show the impulse responses of prices, markups and in\ration | all in percentage deviations from
34:1700:69121:20:20:63:517:622:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:their steady state values | to productivity shocks, distinguishing between the intermediate and
34:1701:69216:20:21:63:517:602:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\fnal production sectors. Throughout these exercises we assume that central banks in the two
34:1702:69308:21:20:63:517:581:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:countries set monetary policy to implement a strict CPI in\ration targeting. Similar results can
34:1703:69404:20:20:63:517:561:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:however be obtained assuming that central banks implement the optimal policy, discussed in
34:1704:69494:20:36:63:142:541:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the next section.
34:1705:69511:36:28:63:312:505:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:6.1  Technology shocks to upstream \frms
34:1706:69551:28:20:63:517:477:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Figure 1 focuses on the e-ects of an unexpected and persistent productivity increase in the Home
34:1707:69647:20:20:63:517:457:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tradable goods sector. Consistent with strict in\ration targeting, the monetary authorities react
34:1708:69744:20:21:63:517:437:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to the shock by expanding the country's monetary stance in line with productivity, causing a
34:1709:69836:21:20:63:517:416:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:depreciation of the nominal exchange rate | given CPI in\ration targeting, the nominal and real
34:1710:69931:20:20:63:454:396:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:exchange rate move together (see the graph in the lower right corner of Figure 1).
34:1711:70013:20:21:80:517:376:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:As shown by Figure 1, upstream producers that update their prices lower them both in the
34:1712:70101:21:20:63:517:355:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:domestic and the foreign market (see the \frst chart on the upper left corner of the \fgure). The
34:1713:70198:20:20:63:517:335:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:fall in the home good price is however larger abroad than in the domestic market, in violation
34:1714:70292:20:21:63:517:315:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the law of one price. In the graph, a positive deviation from the law of one price means that
34:1715:70388:21:20:63:281:294:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:domestic prices are larger than foreign prices.
34:1716:70435:20:20:80:517:274:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The behavior of prices is mirrored by the response of the desired and actual markups of the
34:1717:70526:20:21:63:517:254:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:upstream Home producers, shown by the fourth and \ffth graphs of Figure 1. As discussed in
34:1718:70616:21:20:63:517:233:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Section 4, downstream nominal rigidities lead to pricing substitutability at the level of upstream
34:1719:70714:20:20:63:517:213:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:producers. As a result, thedesired markupby these producers fall with their prices in either
34:1720:70806:20:21:63:517:193:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:market, but relatively more in the Foreign one.15Nonetheless, since prices are sticky in local
34:1721:70900:21:20:63:517:172:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:currency, the nominal depreciation of the Home exchange rate raises export revenues in the
34:1722:70990:20:16:63:420:152:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:exporters' own currency: theaverage markupin the country actually rises.
34:1723:71062:16:20:72:517:136:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:15Recall that we also show that this result is attenuated when the production function include local labor input,
34:1724:71175:20:0:63:365:116:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:with a low degree of substitutability with the intermediate tradable goods.
35:1725:71252:0:20:80:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The impact of the same shock onconsumer pricesclearly di-ers, depending on whether the
35:1726:71338:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:upstream monopolist in a particular industryhupdates its price, or leaves it unchanged. In
35:1727:71428:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the former case (shown in the second graph of Figure 1), downstream \frms face a drop in their
35:1728:71522:21:20:63:517:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:marginal costs. Hence, those \frms which can reset prices will lower them, both domestically
35:1729:71614:20:20:63:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and abroad. As we have seen previously, the intermediate good price falls more in the Foreign
35:1730:71707:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:country. Thus, Foreign downstream \frms decrease their price by more than the domestic ones,
35:1731:71799:21:20:63:517:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:so that deviations from the law of one price have the same sign at both consumer prices' and
35:1732:71891:20:20:63:167:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:producer prices' level.
35:1733:71914:20:21:80:517:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Interestingly, our results show that consumer prices fall also in industries in which the up-
35:1734:72007:21:20:63:517:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:stream producersdo notupdate their prices during the period | albeit by a smaller amount
35:1735:72095:20:20:63:517:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:than in the other case (see the third graph of Figure 1).  This is so for two reasons.  First,
35:1736:72189:20:21:63:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:although marginal costs of downstream \frms in these industry do not fall in the period, these
35:1737:72283:21:20:63:517:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\frms nonetheless take into account that the productivity shock is persistent: they thus antici-
35:1738:72379:20:20:63:517:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:pate that their marginal costs are likely to decrease in the future. Second, a lower price helps
35:1739:72475:20:21:63:517:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:these \frms respond to increasing competition by \frms operating in the other industries, where
35:1740:72570:21:20:63:343:409:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the price of intermediate product have already gone down.
35:1741:72627:20:20:80:517:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:In these industries, the deviations from the law of one price are larger, but of the opposite
35:1742:72720:20:21:63:517:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:sign, relative to the industries in which the upstream price is updated. This is because, for a
35:1743:72815:21:20:63:517:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:constant upstream price, consumer prices decrease on impact by more at Home than abroad.
35:1744:72903:20:20:63:517:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:To wit: in the \frst period, the sign of the deviations from the law of one price is positive in the
35:1745:73003:20:36:63:320:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:second graph, negative in the third graph of Figure 1.
35:1746:73057:36:28:63:328:272:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:6.2  Technology shocks to downstream \frms
35:1747:73099:28:20:63:517:244:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Figure 2 displays the responses to an unexpected persistent increase in the productivity of Home
35:1748:73195:20:20:63:517:224:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:downstream \frms. As in the previous case, under the assumed strict CPI in\ration targeting the
35:1749:73290:20:21:63:517:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Home monetary authorities react with an expansion, which leads to nominal and real deprecia-
35:1750:73382:21:20:63:326:183:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tion of the Home currency (see last graph of Figure 2).
35:1751:73437:20:20:80:517:163:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Recall that downstream technology shocks are also country-speci\fc: they lower the marginal
35:1752:73528:20:21:63:517:143:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:costs of downstream \frms at Home, but do not a-ect the costs of downstream \frms in the
35:1753:73616:21:20:63:517:122:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:industry located in the Foreign country. So, in all industries in which the upstream producers
35:1754:73710:20:0:63:517:102:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:do not update their current price within the period, domestic downstream \frms updating their
36:1755:73805:0:20:63:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:prices will optimally lower them, while downstream \frms abroad will keep their prices virtually
36:1756:73901:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:unchanged. This is at the root of the deviations from the law of one price shown in the third
36:1757:73994:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:graph of Figure 2, which are further magni\fed by the fact that monetary authorities react to
36:1758:74087:21:20:63:322:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the shock by engineering Home currency depreciation.
36:1759:74139:20:20:80:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:More complex is the case of industries in which upstream producers change their prices (sec-
36:1760:74231:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ond graph in the Figure), since the overall e-ects of the shock will depend on a number of general
36:1761:74329:21:20:63:517:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium e-ects. Key to understanding these e-ects is the fact that higher productivity by
36:1762:74422:20:20:63:517:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:downstream \frms causes an increase in their output, and thus in real domestic consumption.
36:1763:74513:20:21:63:517:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:In our model speci\fcation, the increase in downstream output does not a-ect the labor market
36:1764:74606:21:20:63:517:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and thus the real wage directly | under the linear production function speci\fed above, a higher
36:1765:74702:20:20:63:517:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:downstream output has no direct impact on the demand for labor, since these \frms are assumed
36:1766:74795:20:21:63:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:not to employ any labor input. However, it does so indirectly: higher domestic consumption is
36:1767:74888:21:20:63:517:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:associated with a positive income e-ect, which reduces labor supply and ultimately translates
36:1768:74981:20:20:63:517:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:into a downward shift in hours worked. Given that at the same time the demand for intermediate
36:1769:75075:20:21:63:517:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:products is increasing, the labor market tightens, causing a rise in real wages. Facing higher
36:1770:75169:21:20:63:517:409:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:labor costs, upstream \frms which can reoptimize their prices raise them, thus increasing the
36:1771:75262:20:20:63:517:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:marginal costs of downstream \frms. Somewhat surprisingly, as shown in the second graph of
36:1772:75352:20:21:63:347:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Figure 2, the feedback e-ect on consumer prices is positive.
36:1773:75412:21:20:80:517:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:This transmission mechanism was discussed early on by Friedman, in his celebrated critical
36:1774:75502:20:20:63:517:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:analysis of cost-push in\ration (see e.g. Nelson [2007] and references within). In the industries
36:1775:75599:20:21:63:517:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:where upstream producers adjust their prices, they raise them in response to higher costs in
36:1776:75691:21:20:63:517:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the form of higher nominal wages. Yet, one key factor raising wages is the demand expansion
36:1777:75782:20:20:63:517:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:engineered by monetary policy makers in response to productivity improvement at retail level.
36:1778:75875:20:21:63:517:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Changes in prices which appear to be motivated by costs consideration, are actually the result
36:1779:75969:21:20:63:517:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of a demand stimulus, working its way up through the vertical links between downstream and
36:1780:76059:20:20:63:517:206:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:upstream producers, and ultimately raising the price of scarse production inputs supplied in
36:1781:76151:20:21:63:163:186:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:competitive markets.
36:1782:76171:21:20:80:517:165:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Observe that domestic upstream producers slightly lower their wholesale prices in foreign
36:1783:76260:20:20:63:517:145:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:currency.  Nonetheless, because of currency depreciation, these prices in Home currency are
36:1784:76351:20:21:63:517:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:higher than the ones charged in the domestic market, again in violation of the law of one price.
36:1785:76447:21:0:63:517:104:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Consistently, the desired markup of Home producers increases in the Home market, while falls
37:1786:76541:0:20:63:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:abroad | in line with the change in prices. The average markup nonetheless falls everywhere
37:1787:76632:20:43:63:288:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the economy, per e-ect of nominal rigidities.
37:1788:76680:43:32:63:478:651:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:7  International dimensions of optimal stabilization policy
37:1789:76739:32:20:63:517:619:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:This section is devoted to the analysis of stabilization policies under the assumption of coopera-
37:1790:76837:20:20:63:517:599:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tion between the Home and Foreign monetary authorities and full commitment. In order to shed
37:1791:76929:20:21:63:517:579:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:light on how policy works in our model, we \fnd it useful to discuss the problem of stabilizing
37:1792:77024:21:20:63:517:558:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:economies hit by shocks to upstream or downstream shocks in isolation, and then proceed to
37:1793:77114:20:20:63:517:538:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:present results for our complete baseline calibration. Thus, results are shown in 3 tables. For a
37:1794:77211:20:21:63:517:518:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:set of macrovariables, Table 1 and 2 report volatilities conditional on shocks to upstream and
37:1795:77305:21:20:63:517:497:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:downstream productivity, respectively; Table 3 report results when both shocks are considered.
37:1796:77399:20:20:63:517:477:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:In each table, the \frst column shows result for the \rexible price benchmark, in which monetary
37:1797:77495:20:21:63:517:457:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:policy targets a zero rate of CPI in\ration at all times; the other columns refer to economies
37:1798:77589:21:20:63:517:436:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:with price rigidities under di-erent policy regimes.  Tables 1 and 2 only show results under
37:1799:77681:20:20:63:517:416:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the optimal cooperative policy, including a case in which there is no home bias in consumption
37:1800:77775:20:20:63:517:396:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:expenditure (i.e.aH=aF= 1=2). Table 3, instead, includes the alternative monetary policies
37:1801:77865:20:21:63:517:376:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:speci\fed in Section 5 | CPI in\ration targeting, GDP in\ration targeting, and the Taylor-type
37:1802:77959:21:20:63:517:355:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rule. As we assume subsidies that exactly o-set steady-state markups, under the optimal policy
37:1803:78053:20:20:63:517:335:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:long-run in\ration is zero. To facilitate comparison across experiments, we also posit that steady
37:1804:78151:20:37:63:418:315:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:state in\ration is nil when solving the model under the alternative policies.
37:1805:78228:37:27:63:223:278:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:7.1  Upstream shocks only
37:1806:78253:27:20:63:517:251:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Starting from the simplest case, consider \frst the problem of stabilizing technology shocks to
37:1807:78348:20:21:63:517:231:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:upstream production only. As an important benchmark, we \frst establish that, if our Home
37:1808:78437:21:20:63:517:210:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:country were a closed economy, monetary authorities would be able to stabilize completely
37:1809:78526:20:20:63:517:190:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:upstream marginal costs, and therefore upstream prices, preventing any dispersion in the prices
37:1810:78621:20:21:63:517:170:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:charged by adjusting and not-adjusting \frms. Monetary authorities can do so by matching any
37:1811:78713:21:20:63:517:149:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:change in upstream marginal costs driven by productivity, with a change in the monetary stance
37:1812:78807:20:20:63:517:129:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in the opposite direction, which ultimately moves nominal wages in tandem with productivity.
37:1813:78899:20:0:63:517:109:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The speci\fc reason why such a policy would stabilize all sticky prices (at both producer and
38:1814:78994:0:20:63:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consumer level) is that, in our speci\fcation, \ructuations in nominal wages are not consequential
38:1815:79092:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for downstream \frms, by virtue of our assumption that these \frms employ no labor resources in
38:1816:79187:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:producing \fnal goods. So, downstream marginal costs only change with the intermediate goods'
38:1817:79280:21:20:63:517:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:prices, or with downstream productivity: without shocks to the latter, once upstream prices are
38:1818:79375:20:20:63:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:constant in equilibrium, so are downstream prices. Similarly to the standard closed-economy
38:1819:79466:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:monetary model, the policy just described would replicate the allocation under \rexible prices
38:1820:79560:21:20:63:517:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:| this policy is optimal in our environment since we assume that steady-state monopolistic
38:1821:79650:20:20:63:370:572:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:distortions in production are corrected with \fscal instruments.16
38:1822:79716:20:21:80:517:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The optimality of complete price stabilization, however, does not carry over to an open
38:1823:79803:21:20:63:517:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:economy setting, as shown in Table 1. With an optimal monetary policy in place (second column
38:1824:79896:20:20:63:517:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the table), the variability of the CPI is close to, but not zero | domestic and imported goods
38:1825:79993:20:21:63:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:prices are actually much more variable than the CPI. Observe that prices and markups in both
38:1826:80085:21:20:63:517:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:countries \ructuate much less for domestic goods than for imported goods. This corresponds to
38:1827:80178:20:20:63:517:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the fact that monetary policymakers concentrate their e-orts to reduce the volatility of markups
38:1828:80274:20:21:63:517:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of domestic producers selling in the domestic markets. The reason has already been laid out in
38:1829:80368:21:20:63:517:409:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Section 2.1, but is worth reconsidering here in the framework of our model with staggered price
38:1830:80463:20:20:63:98:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:setting.
38:1831:80471:20:21:80:517:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:By mirroring the logic of Corsetti and Pesenti [2005], assume an equilibrium where there is
38:1832:80562:21:20:63:517:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:no price dispersion in either domestic market for domestically produced goods: the monetary
38:1833:80653:20:20:63:517:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:authority completely stabilizes the marginal costs ofupstream\frms, once again matching any
38:1834:80744:20:21:63:517:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:increase in productivity with an appropriate expansion in the Home monetary stance. While do-
38:1835:80837:21:16:63:517:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:mestic goods prices remain constant and identical to each other, at both intermediate and \fnal
38:1836:80932:16:20:72:517:271:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:16It is worth stressing that, had we assumed that downstream \frms use labor, complete stability of upstream
38:1837:81040:20:16:63:517:251:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:prices would be incompatible with complete stability of downstream prices. Even if prices of intermediate goods
38:1838:81151:16:17:63:517:235:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:were held constant, movements in nominal wages in response to endogenous monetary policy changes would ad-
38:1839:81257:17:16:63:517:218:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:ditionally a-ect marginal costs of \fnal good producers, creating an immediate incentive for these to reset prices
38:1840:81371:16:17:63:517:202:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:when possible, thus generating price variability at the retail level. As a result, relative to our baseline model spec-
38:1841:81490:17:16:63:517:185:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:i\fcation, introducing a labor input in \fnal good production implies that welfare maximizing monetary authorities
38:1842:81604:16:16:63:517:169:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:would face a trade-o- between stabilization of upstream marginal costs, and downstream price dispersion. They
38:1843:81713:16:17:63:517:153:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:would therefore tend to react by less to upstream productivity shocks, with the objective of containing price
38:1844:81822:17:16:63:517:136:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:dispersion at consumer level. As should become clear in the rest of the text, abstracting from labor inputs in
38:1845:81932:16:17:63:517:120:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:downstream production is helpful in focusing most sharply on the policy trade-o-s arising speci\fcally from vertical
38:1846:82048:17:0:63:281:103:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:interactions between downstream and upstream \frms.
39:1847:82101:0:20:63:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:level, any monetary decision a-ecting the nominal exchange rate would create both a misalign-
39:1848:82194:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ment of the relative price between domestic and foreign goods, and import price dispersion at
39:1849:82287:20:21:63:516:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consumer level (since a fraction-of Foreign producers would react to, e.g., Home depreciation,
39:1850:82381:21:20:63:412:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:by ine-ciently raising the price they charge to Home downstream \frms).
39:1851:82452:20:20:80:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:At the margin, depending on the degree of openness of the economy, it would be optimal
39:1852:82538:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to move away from such outcome.  Speci\fcally, it is e-cient to stabilize the marginal costs
39:1853:82630:21:20:63:517:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of domestic intermediate producers by less, as to stabilize somewhat marginal costs and thus
39:1854:82722:20:20:63:517:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:reduce the incentive to move prices in the import sector. Monetary authorities can raise welfare
39:1855:82818:20:21:63:517:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:by trading-o- lower import price dispersion and misalignment at the consumer level, against
39:1856:82909:21:20:63:365:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:some price dispersion in the Home markets for domestic goods.
39:1857:82970:20:20:80:517:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We observe here that optimal Foreign monetary policy would mimic Home monetary policy
39:1858:83055:20:21:63:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in response to Home shocks, for essentially the same reason.  For a given Foreign monetary
39:1859:83145:21:20:63:517:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:policy, a Home currency depreciation generates price variability in local currency of Foreign
39:1860:83238:20:20:63:517:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:imports from Home, as Home exporters updating their price will lower them. An expansion
39:1861:83325:20:21:63:517:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:allows the Foreign monetary authorities to contain the variability of import prices, as well as
39:1862:83420:21:20:63:517:409:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:their misalignment relative to the domestic goods prices, at the cost of some price dispersion in
39:1863:83517:20:20:63:517:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the domestic market for domestic goods. This is exactly what underlies our numerical results
39:1864:83609:20:21:63:114:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in Table 1.
39:1865:83620:21:20:80:517:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:As is well understood in the literature, with LCP, endogenous changes in monetary stance
39:1866:83708:20:20:63:517:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:across countries tend to be positively correlated. In the limiting case in which there is no home
39:1867:83805:20:21:63:517:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:bias in consumption (the case reported in the third column in Table 1), domestic and foreign
39:1868:83897:21:20:63:517:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:goods in the Home and the Foreign consumer price indexes have exactly the same weights.
39:1869:83984:20:20:63:517:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:This implies that, in response to disturbances to upstream productivity, national monetary
39:1870:84074:20:21:63:517:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:policy stances react to the same weighted average of shocks, becoming perfectly correlated in
39:1871:84167:21:20:63:517:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the optimum. As a result, the nominal exchange rate does not respond to shocks (in the third
39:1872:84259:20:20:63:517:206:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:column of Table 1, the volatility of the real exchange rate is 0), even if shocks are country-speci\fc
39:1873:84361:20:21:63:517:186:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and uncorrelated | a \fnding discussed at length by the literature surveyed in Section 2. What
39:1874:84455:21:20:63:517:165:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:induces optimal exchange rate variability under cooperation is home bias in consumption, which
39:1875:84549:20:20:63:517:145:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:obviously raises the importance of stabilizing the marginal costs of domestic producers relative
39:1876:84645:20:21:63:517:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to those of the importers (the case shown in the second column in Table 1). In this respect, our
39:1877:84741:21:0:63:517:104:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:results generalize the point discussed by Corsetti [2006] to an environment with staggered price
40:1878:84839:0:20:63:119:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:adjustment.
40:1879:84850:20:20:80:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:By comparing the \frst and the second column of Table 1, it is apparent that the positive co-
40:1880:84943:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f7:B:movements in optimal national monetary policies induced by LCP distortions curb thevolatility
40:1881:85036:21:20:63:516:653:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f3:B:of the terms of trade,relative to the case of \rexible prices. With LCP, nominal exchange rate
40:1882:85130:20:20:63:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:movements do not help correct international relative prices. The only way in which a nominal
40:1883:85222:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:expansion cum exchange rate depreciation can reduce the price of domestic goods sold abroad
40:1884:85313:21:20:63:517:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is via price adjustment in foreign currency, but by the Calvo mechanism only a subset of \frms
40:1885:85407:20:20:63:517:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:can reduce their prices. For all the other \frms, the terms of trade actually move in the direction
40:1886:85506:20:21:63:517:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of an appreciation.  In other words, while exchange rate movements induced by a monetary
40:1887:85594:21:20:63:517:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:expansion have nothing to do with expenditure switching e-ects, a fall in the relative price of
40:1888:85689:20:20:63:517:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:imports can only materialize at the cost of import price dispersion.  This is why, depending
40:1889:85781:20:21:63:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:on the relative weight of domestic and imported goods in the CPI, optimal stabilization policy
40:1890:85875:21:20:63:445:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tends to contain international relative prices and thus terms of trade variability.
40:1891:85958:20:20:80:517:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:However, observe that in our results the volatility of the real exchange rate, like that of
40:1892:86049:20:21:63:517:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:consumption and hours worked, is higher with nominal rigidities (under the optimal policy),
40:1893:86140:21:20:63:517:409:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:than with \rexible prices | the opposite of our results on the terms of trade. We will return on
40:1894:86236:20:36:63:195:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:this important point below.
40:1895:86263:36:28:63:239:353:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:7.2  Downstream shocks only
40:1896:86290:28:20:63:517:325:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Shocks hitting \fnal good producers substantially modify the monetary policy problem, in at least
40:1897:86387:20:20:63:517:305:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:two respects. First, in our baseline speci\fcation without labor input in downstream production,
40:1898:86483:20:21:63:517:285:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:monetary authorities would never be able to achieve complete stability of \fnal prices, not even
40:1899:86579:21:20:63:517:264:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in a closed-economy environment. In other words, these shocks create policy trade-o-s among
40:1900:86670:20:20:63:517:244:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:competing objective independently of openness. The problem is that complete price stability
40:1901:86761:20:20:63:517:224:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:at consumer level requires monetary policy to respond to technology shocks downstream. Since
40:1902:86853:20:21:63:517:204:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the resulting \ructuations in wages (see Section 6.2) induce (ine-cient) price dispersion among
40:1903:86948:21:20:63:517:183:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:upstream \frms, it follows that \fnal producers will face di-erent costs of their intermediate input,
40:1904:87049:20:20:63:517:163:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:depending on which industry they operate in. In this sense, vertical interactions in our model
40:1905:87143:20:21:63:517:143:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:bring about an important dimension of heterogeneity across \frms which should be appropriately
40:1906:87237:21:20:63:517:122:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:emphasized. Di-erently from standard sticky price models, the marginal costs of our downstream
40:1907:87331:20:0:63:517:102:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\frms are generally not symmetric, not even when the economy is completely closed to foreign
41:1908:87425:0:20:63:416:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:trade, and there are no markup shocks, due e.g. to stochastic preferences.
41:1909:87499:20:20:80:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Second, since \fnal producers di-erentiate locally the products they bring to consumers,
41:1910:87587:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:downstream shocks add an important element of nontradability to consumer goods.  Hence,
41:1911:87674:21:20:63:517:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:even when consumer expenditure is not biased towards domestic goods, consumption baskets
41:1912:87762:20:20:63:516:633:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f16:B:would still be e-ectively di-erent across countries. When the expenditure weightsaHandaF
41:1913:87850:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:are identical | a case of no home bias in terms of upstream products | monetary authorities
41:1914:87941:21:20:63:517:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:would e-ciently provide the same degree of stabilization across all categories of domestic and
41:1915:88035:20:20:63:517:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:imported goods. Yet, in contrast to the case of upstream disturbances only, the optimal monetary
41:1916:88131:20:21:63:517:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:stance will be su-ciently di-erent across countries as to induce nominal and real exchange
41:1917:88221:21:20:63:517:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rate \ructuations in response to country-speci\fc shocks at downstream level. This result is a
41:1918:88315:20:20:63:517:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:generalization of Duarte and Obstfeld [2007], who also stress nontradability as a reason for
41:1919:88407:20:21:63:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:nominal exchange rate \rexibility. However, they include nontradables as a separate sector in
41:1920:88500:21:20:63:517:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the economy (as they abstract from vertical interactions), and focus on the case of one period
41:1921:88594:20:20:63:373:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:preset prices (hence abstract from forward looking price setting).
41:1922:88660:20:21:80:517:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The above discussion is clearly re\rected in the results in Table 2. When we focus on down-
41:1923:88751:21:20:63:517:409:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:stream shocks only, the variability of CPI in\ration is not zero, and remains remarkably stable
41:1924:88846:20:20:63:517:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:for di-erent degrees of home bias in consumption. What instead varies considerably with the
41:1925:88937:20:21:63:517:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:degree of home bias is the variability of markups across sectors, since home bias shifts the weight
41:1926:89036:21:20:63:517:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of monetary stabilization away from imported goods. Precisely, observe that in the third col-
41:1927:89129:20:20:63:517:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:umn | the case of no home bias | markups are equally stabilized at the retail level, for both
41:1928:89222:20:21:63:517:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:domestic and foreign goods. In the second column, instead, the markup of \fnal producers is
41:1929:89313:21:20:63:440:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:much less volatile if they sell domestic goods, than if they sell imported goods.
41:1930:89394:20:20:80:517:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Relative to the case of upstream shocks, there are two notable di-erences as regards exchange
41:1931:89487:20:21:63:517:247:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rate volatility. First, because of nontradability, the real exchange rate is now much more volatile
41:1932:89586:21:20:63:517:226:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:than the terms of trade, even in the \rexible price allocation. Second, relative to the \rexible
41:1933:89682:20:20:63:517:206:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:price allocation, an economy with nominal rigidities and the optimal policy in place will be
41:1934:89774:20:21:63:517:186:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:characterized by more volatility in both the real exchange rate and the terms of trade. The fact
41:1935:89870:21:20:63:517:165:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:that these patterns are quite di-erent from those discussed in the previous subsection makes it
41:1936:89965:20:20:63:517:145:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:clear that optimal monetary policies do not translate into any general prescription about the
41:1937:90058:20:0:63:283:125:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:relative volatility of these international prices.
42:1938:90110:0:27:63:198:714:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:7.3  Baseline economy
42:1939:90131:27:20:63:517:687:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:We now have all the basic elements to analyze our baseline economy with all shocks combined.
42:1940:90223:20:21:63:517:667:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Results are shown in Table 3. Observe that the combination of downstream and upstream shocks
42:1941:90315:21:20:63:517:646:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:raises the volatility in our arti\fcial economy reasonably close to the data for the US and other
42:1942:90412:20:20:63:517:626:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:large industrial economies: for instance, the standard deviations of real GDP is (realistically)
42:1943:90508:20:21:63:300:606:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:around 2 percent, regardless of nominal rigidities.
42:1944:90559:21:20:80:517:585:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Consider \frst the \rexible-price benchmark, shown in the \frst column of the table. With
42:1945:90648:20:20:63:517:565:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\rexible prices, the demand elasticity facing producers, and thus the markups they charge, are
42:1946:90742:20:21:63:517:545:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:constant; therefore the law of one price holds at the dock (the volatility of deviations from the law
42:1947:90843:21:20:63:517:524:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of one price at the dock is correspondingly zero). Nonetheless, the law of one price (cannot and)
42:1948:90940:20:20:63:517:504:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:does not hold for \fnal goods: country-speci\fc productivity shocks hitting the downstream \frms
42:1949:91036:20:21:63:517:484:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:drive a wedge between \fnal goods' prices across countries (expressed in a common currency). As
42:1950:91131:21:20:63:517:463:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:a result, and in accord to stylized facts, the real exchange rate is more volatile than the terms
42:1951:91228:20:20:63:517:443:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of trade; the correlation between the real (and nominal) exchange rate is high and positive
42:1952:91319:20:21:63:517:423:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:| despite the fact that upstream and downstream technology shocks are assumed not to be
42:1953:91406:21:20:63:517:402:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:correlated. Recall that, in our \rexible price economy, we posit that monetary policy keeps the
42:1954:91501:20:20:63:517:382:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:CPI constant: consistent with this monetary regime, sectoral in\ration rates are more volatile at
42:1955:91598:20:21:63:517:362:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:producer level than at the \fnal level, and for imported goods than for domestically produced
42:1956:91691:21:20:63:517:341:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:goods, respectively. The latter result clearly re\rects the low weight of foreign goods in the CPI.
42:1957:91790:20:20:80:517:321:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:The second column of Table 3 displays results for our sticky-price economy with the opti-
42:1958:91879:20:21:63:517:301:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:mal policy in place. In order to reduce ine-ciencies due to price stickiness, monetary policy
42:1959:91972:21:20:63:517:280:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:mitigates \ructuations in the major components of consumer price in\ration. However, it falls
42:1960:92065:20:20:63:517:260:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:short of completely stabilizing either the CPI or domestic intermediate prices in\ration. Key
42:1961:92158:20:21:63:517:240:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to understanding this result are the di-erent trade-o-s discussed in the text above. First, as
42:1962:92252:21:20:63:517:219:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in Corsetti and Pesenti [2005], LCP at upstream level leads benevolent monetary authorities
42:1963:92343:20:20:63:517:199:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to attach a positive weight to stabilizing the consumer price of imports, and thus to deviate
42:1964:92436:20:21:63:517:179:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:from perfect stabilization of the \fnal prices of domestic goods. Second, downstream technology
42:1965:92531:21:20:63:517:158:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:shocks prevent perfect stabilization of all consumer prices, because of the heterogeneity of mar-
42:1966:92628:20:20:63:517:138:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ginal costs implied by vertical interactions. This e-ect is of course worse in an open economy
42:1967:92722:20:0:63:517:118:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:setting, because of the response of the intermediate price of imports to exchange rate \ructua-
43:1968:92819:0:20:63:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tions. Third, the elasticity of the producer's demand curve depends on the industry's dispersion
43:1969:92915:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of \fnal goods prices, motivating policy emphasis on \fnal price stabilization. The implications
43:1970:93011:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of these trade-o-s for the volatilities of prices and markups, real exchange rates and terms of
43:1971:93106:21:20:63:517:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:trade are discussed below, together with a comparative analysis of the optimal policy relative
43:1972:93200:20:36:63:163:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to other policy rules.
43:1973:93222:36:20:63:517:597:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f3:B:Prices and markupsBecause of limited price adjustment, it is not surprising that real vari-
43:1974:93313:20:20:63:517:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:ables generally display more volatility in the sticky-price economy (with the optimal monetary
43:1975:93407:20:21:63:516:557:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:policy in place), than in the \rexible-price economy.17Notable exceptions are the terms of trade
43:1976:93503:21:20:63:517:536:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and hours worked. The reduced volatility of the terms of trade is a consequence of LCP at the
43:1977:93596:20:20:63:517:516:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:intermediate level, as discussed in Section 7.1 above. A reduced volatility of hours worked is
43:1978:93690:20:21:63:517:496:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:already a feature of optimal monetary policy with downstream shocks only in Table 2, and is
43:1979:93781:21:20:63:491:475:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:essentially a consequences of our assumption that downstream \frms do not employ labor.
43:1980:93868:20:20:80:517:455:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:What is most interesting, instead, is the very large discrepancy in volatilities of producers'
43:1981:93962:20:21:63:517:435:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:and distributors' average markups, which are constant in the \rexible-price allocation.  The
43:1982:94054:21:20:63:517:414:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:markup of domestically produced goods is two and a half times as volatile at the upstream level
43:1983:94149:20:20:63:517:394:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:as at the downstream level. This is remarkable in light of the fact that, in our experiments, we
43:1984:94245:20:21:63:517:374:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:assume the same degree of nominal rigidities at either level. The volatility di-erential re\rects the
43:1985:94346:21:20:63:517:353:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:real components of markup movements in producers' prices, arising from vertical interactions.
43:1986:94439:20:20:63:517:333:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Conversely, the markup of imported goods is more volatile at the downstream level than at the
43:1987:94532:20:21:63:517:313:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:upstream level | almost twice as much. Such di-erential re\rects the fact that optimal policy
43:1988:94625:21:20:63:517:292:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:attaches a large weight to stabilizing domestically produced goods at the retail level | the bulk
43:1989:94722:20:20:63:197:272:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of households' consumption.
43:1990:94749:20:21:80:517:252:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:We should stress here that \ructuations in markups translate into ine-cient deviations in the
43:1991:94842:21:20:63:517:231:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:law of one price, both at the border and at the consumer level. Observe that the volatility of
43:1992:94936:20:16:63:517:211:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:deviations from the law of one price in \fnal prices is quite similar to the one in the economy with
43:1993:95036:16:20:72:517:195:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:17The volatility di-erential between our economies with and without nominal rigidities is by no means uniform
43:1994:95145:20:16:63:517:175:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:across sectors. Namely, for domestically produced goods, the ratio in volatility of upstream and downstream prices
43:1995:95259:16:17:63:517:159:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:is 4 in the \rexible price allocation, but it falls down to 2.5 with nominal rigidities. A similar drop can be found in
43:1996:95378:17:16:63:517:142:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:the ratio of volatility of imports prices to domestic goods prices. Conversely, the volatility of the producer price
43:1997:95494:16:17:63:517:126:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:of imported goods, though lower than in the \rexible price economy, is now twice that of domestically produced
43:1998:95604:17:0:63:89:109:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:goods.
44:1999:95612:0:20:63:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:\rexible prices, notwithstanding that, per e-ect of the exchange rate movements, the markups
44:2000:95704:20:36:63:432:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of Home downstream \frms selling imported goods have the highest volatility.
44:2001:95780:36:20:63:517:658:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f3:B:Real exchange rates and terms of tradeA notable international dimension of the optimal
44:2002:95866:20:20:63:517:638:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:policy in Table 3 is that the real exchange rate is more volatile in the economy with nominal
44:2003:95959:20:21:63:517:618:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:frictions than under \rexible prices, while the terms of trade is less volatile, re\recting the e-ects
44:2004:96061:21:20:63:517:597:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of LCP and nontradability discussed above. These \fndings clearly caution against suggestions
44:2005:96154:20:20:63:517:577:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to drastically curb the volatility of nominal and real exchange rates. For instance, they caution
44:2006:96251:20:21:63:517:557:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:against the strong policy prescription derived by by Devereux and Engel [2007], who argue that
44:2007:96345:21:20:63:517:536:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:under pervasive LCP the optimal stabilization policy should reduce the variability of the real
44:2008:96439:20:20:63:517:516:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:exchange rate signi\fcantly below that of the terms of trade. In these authors' view, the fact that
44:2009:96538:20:21:63:517:496:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:we observe the opposite pattern in the data suggests that policymakers around the world fail to
44:2010:96633:21:20:63:517:475:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:stabilize currency movements e-ciently. As we argued above, the problem with this and similar
44:2011:96726:20:20:63:517:455:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:views is that, while there are good theoretical reasons to expect optimal policies under LCP to
44:2012:96821:20:21:63:517:435:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:contain the volatility of the terms of trade, these reasons cannot be mechanically applied to the
44:2013:96918:21:20:63:517:414:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:real exchange rate, whose volatility is bound to depend on a number of structural features of
44:2014:97011:20:36:63:133:394:11:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:B:the economy.18
44:2015:97025:36:20:63:517:358:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f3:B:Simple rulesThe last three columns of Table 3 report results for alternative policy rules,
44:2016:97115:20:20:63:517:338:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:namely, CPI in\ration targeting, GDP in\ration targeting and a standard Taylor rule. Compared
44:2017:97208:20:20:63:517:318:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to the optimal policy, these alternative simple rules bring about noticeably larger volatility in
44:2018:97305:20:21:63:517:298:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:most real variables, particularly in the markups and the deviations from the law of one price for
44:2019:97402:21:20:63:278:277:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:both consumer prices and prices at the dock.
44:2020:97446:20:20:80:517:257:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Focus \frst on the strict CPI in\ration targeting regime, presented in the third column of
44:2021:97536:20:21:63:517:237:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:Table 3: such monetary policy regime leads to more volatility in the upstream prices of all
44:2022:97627:21:20:63:517:216:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:goods (imported and domestically produced).  Relative to the optimal policy, the economy
44:2023:97715:20:20:63:517:196:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:displays higher volatility of markups, terms of trade and the real exchange rate.  This is so
44:2024:97808:20:16:63:517:176:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:because complete stabilization of headline consumer price in\ration brings about suboptimally
44:2025:97901:16:21:72:517:160:6:g_d0_f5:9:g_d0_f6:F:18As discussed above, in our model the optimal ranking of volatility between the real exchange rate and the
44:2026:98008:21:16:63:517:139:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:terms of trade depends, among other things, on the relative degree of price stickiness among upstream and
44:2027:98113:16:16:63:517:123:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:downstream producers. If producer prices are assumed to be completely \rexible, the real exchange rate becomes
44:2028:98223:16:0:63:470:107:9:g_d0_f6:9:g_d0_f6:F:less volatile than the terms of trade | in line with the case discussed by Devereux and Engel [2007].
45:2029:98326:0:20:63:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:large movements in sectoral (i.e. domestic and imported goods) in\ration rates at retail level,
45:2030:98421:20:20:63:389:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:which ultimately a-ect the desired markups by upstream producers.
45:2031:98486:20:21:80:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Likewise, stabilizing the prices of domestically produced goods | the case dubbed GDP
45:2032:98571:21:20:63:517:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in\ration targeting in the fourth column of Table 3 | also leads to too much volatility in sectoral
45:2033:98670:20:20:63:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in\ration rates, especially in in\ration of imported goods at the border as well as at the consumer
45:2034:98769:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:level. Interestingly, consumption and real GDP are less volatile than under the optimal policy;
45:2035:98864:21:20:63:517:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:but this is achieved by generating more volatility in all other real variables, especially in hours
45:2036:98963:20:20:63:517:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:worked and in the terms of trade, because of the suboptimally low weight attached to stabilizing
45:2037:99059:20:21:63:216:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:export and import goods prices.
45:2038:99090:21:20:80:517:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, a Taylor rule (following a quite standard parameterization) improves on the strict
45:2039:99181:20:20:63:517:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:CPI in\ration target, by producing less volatility in consumption and hours. However, relative
45:2040:99275:20:21:63:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to the optimal policy, both the CPI and its individual components are too volatile, since too
45:2041:99368:21:20:63:517:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:much importance is attached to output stabilization. As a result, the volatility of consumption
45:2042:99463:20:43:63:238:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:is excessive, that of hours is too low.
45:2043:99502:43:31:63:229:407:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:8  Concluding remarks
45:2044:99523:31:21:63:517:376:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:The literature in international economics and open macro has so far pursued two distinct expla-
45:2045:99618:21:20:63:517:355:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:nations of the observed stability of import prices in local currency. According to one modeling
45:2046:99713:20:20:63:517:335:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:strategy, this is the result of optimal markup adjustment by monopolistic \frms, which optimize
45:2047:99808:20:21:63:517:315:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:pro\fts through price discrimination across national markets. In this case, market segmenta-
45:2048:99900:21:20:63:517:294:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:tion is attributed to real factors. According to an alternative modeling strategy, local-currency
45:2049:99997:20:20:63:517:274:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:price-stability re\rects nominal rigidities, which imply suboptimal variations in \frms pro\fts in
45:2050:100095:20:21:63:517:254:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:response to shocks. By considering vertically integrated \frms, our paper emphasizes that a rigid
45:2051:100192:21:20:63:517:233:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:distinction between these two approaches is unwarranted, since optimal markup adjustments and
45:2052:100285:20:20:63:517:213:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:nominal frictions are likely to act as intertwined factors in causing stable import prices in local
45:2053:100384:20:21:63:517:193:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:currency.  Speci\fcally, we build a model where, because of market-speci\fc nominal rigidities
45:2054:100478:21:20:63:517:172:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:at the downstream level, di-erent dynamics in \fnal prices provide an incentive for upstream
45:2055:100570:20:20:63:517:152:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:producers to price discriminate across countries, exacerbating the distortions from monopoly
45:2056:100662:20:21:63:517:132:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:power. At the same time, the use of local nontradable inputs by \frms selling goods to \fnal
45:2057:100754:21:0:63:391:111:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:users mutes the response of \fnal prices to exchange rate movements.
46:2058:100824:0:20:80:517:714:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:There are at least three potentially important implications of our \fndings for policymaking.
46:2059:100917:20:20:63:517:694:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:First, by creating price discrimination at the border, consumer price movements feed back to
46:2060:101009:20:21:63:517:674:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:deviations from the law of one price across markets. The transmission mechanism from consumer
46:2061:101102:21:20:63:517:653:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:price in\ration to price discrimination provides monetary authorities with an additional reason
46:2062:101197:20:20:63:517:633:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:to stabilize \fnal prices. In this respect, our analysis sheds light on one possible reason why the
46:2063:101296:20:21:63:517:613:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:progressive stabilization of in\ration in the last decade may have contributed to the observed
46:2064:101390:21:20:63:517:592:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:fall in exchange-rate pass-through. By reducing movements in consumer prices, policymakers
46:2065:101480:20:20:63:517:572:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:indirectly a-ect the demand elasticity faced by upstream producers, reducing opportunities for
46:2066:101574:20:21:63:334:552:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:exercising monopoly power through price discrimination.
46:2067:101629:21:20:80:517:531:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Yet, complete CPI stabilization will never be desirable in our economies, because of both
46:2068:101718:20:20:63:517:511:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:international and domestic policy trade-o-s. Speci\fcally, in addition to the international di-
46:2069:101813:20:21:63:517:491:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:mensions of monetary policy already discussed in the literature, we show that, with vertical
46:2070:101905:21:20:63:517:470:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:interactions among industries adjusting prices in a staggered fashion, domestic price stability is
46:2071:102003:20:20:63:517:450:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:actually unfeasible. This is due to the fact that nominal rigidities inducing staggered pricing by
46:2072:102101:20:21:63:465:430:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:upstream producers, inherently lead to cost heterogeneity among downstream \frms.
46:2073:102182:21:20:80:517:409:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, as shown by the literature, nominal rigidities in local currency induce positive co-
46:2074:102275:20:20:63:517:389:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:movements in the optimal monetary stance across countries, which tend to curb the volatility of
46:2075:102370:20:21:63:517:369:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:the terms of trade. However, our results make it clear that, at an optimum, the real exchange
46:2076:102463:21:20:63:517:348:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:rate can be more or less volatile than the terms of trade, depending on a number of structural
46:2077:102557:20:20:63:517:328:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:features of the economy, like home bias in expenditure and local components of marginal costs
46:2078:102650:20:21:63:517:308:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:in consumer goods. In this sense, the empirical regularity that real exchange rates are typically
46:2079:102747:21:20:63:517:287:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:more volatile than the terms of trade does not automatically suggest that policymakers fall short
46:2080:102844:20:43:63:249:267:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:of stabilizing exchange rates e-ciently.
46:2081:102884:43:31:63:156:224:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:9  Appendix
46:2082:102895:31:21:63:517:193:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:B:In this appendix we provide details on the derivation of a few results used extensively in the
